RATING: 5
Very similar to Werewolf but I much prefer the latter one. In Resistance the dynamics of the group does not evolve throughout the game since no characters get killed. Once you have worked out who the bad guys are, it's a simple task for the good to win.  I also find kind of lame that the only way the good players get to contribute to the outcome of the game is the voting for the group that goes out for a mission. In werewolf you at least get to execute other players.

I guess that the designers wanted to have a Werewolf without player elimination but at the same time you agree with sacrificing the very best part of the game. Must be that I am a werewolf.

RATING: 8.5
I don't usually enjoy social deduction games, but this is for sure the best one I've played so far. My biggest complaint about this kind of game is the usual absence of a solid mechanic beneath all the talking, lying and bluffing... which makes the game-play too intangible - so to speak - for me, since the players can only rely on their ability to read other people's faces.

The Resistance is different, even if it's still really simple and straight-forward. The key to its trick is the addition of the voting phase, because it really allows to read the other players's intentions and brings a huge deal of discussion to the table every time. This simple mechanic makes the game very deep and interesting! I also like the fact that all the players are involved at all times... unlike Werewolf, a game which is often compared to Resistance, where players are killed off turn by turn.

The Resistance is a really great game... and one I'm growing more fond of play after play. The Avalon version introduces some really cool roles, that make thing even more interesting and even more tense! Finally I've found the social deduction game that I enjoy. Huge thumbs up for me!

RATING: 10
The Resistance is fantastic with an energetic group of folks and the roles work so much better than the plot cards from the base game. They add information to the game in a more predictable, organized way, and they help folks realize the information and strategy inherent in the game.

I still think that, regardless, there is a lot of data to process (and that the first mission team shouldn't automatically be accepted and that the first mission should necessarily automatically succeed or whatever), but the roles do help this reality set in.

It does, as many games of this ilk, suffer if all players aren't all expressive, and the less sociable can get a bit suppressed, but otherwise great fun.

RATING: 8
The Resistance is a game modeled on Werewolf but with more information on which to base your deduction, no player elimination, and no need for a GM.  Which is all  good in my book. Avalon adds the Merlin character, who operates like the Seer and makes this version even more Werewolfy.  I have found both versions of The Resistance somewhat fragile.  If luck gifts one side an early advantage, it can be over quickly and unsatisfactorily.  On the other hand, it frequently delivers as concentrated a shot of bluff, deduction, paranoia and double-think as you can reasonably expect of a thirty-minute filler.

I rather liked the futuristic resistance cell setting of the original and this Arthurian re-theming makes somewhat less sense.  The art and production are both good.  The rules are clear enough.

RATING: 9
The Resistance is one of my favourite games and Avalon is even better, with nicer components, gorgeous artwork and some interesting options and twists with Merlin and the Assassin adding extra tension.

For those not familiar with The Resistance, Avalon is a social deduction game where players assume secret identities competing as teams to either cause missions to succeed or fail.  The best 3 of 5 wins for the particular side.  

Deceptively simple on the surface, easy to setup and a breeze to learn, the real fun comes from the player interaction involving accusations and bluffing as each person tries (with very limited information) to determine who are the good guys and who are the bad guys.  Works best in a group willing to "talk it up" and I guarantee you'll spend twice as long afterwards laughing and dissecting the tactics and accusations.

Small, cheap with a play-time of around 15-20 mins (depending on group chatter), it covers groups from 5-10 players with no player elimination.  Avalon is a hands down winner and one of those rare games that is as near to perfect as I can find.

RATING: 8
I may be jumping the gun a little here putting this straight into my top 10. I’ve only played the original Resistance a handful of times and thought it was an average game. I’d played it in the past at my local game club and never really considered purchasing it. Then one week I sat down and out this came. I knew nothing of it. After about 3 or 4 games I loved it! 

All the little faults I didn’t like about the original have gone. The components could have been better. You’ll age the cards by just looking at them. This rating has the potential to go up or down. I’m not very experienced with the game, its intricacies and how it will hold up to repeated plays with roughly the same group so I doubt it will settle here.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.7
When we first started playing Resistance, it was at restaurants with a plain deck of cards (black means good and red means spy.) I didn't even know that it was an official, published game--this was before I was even aware of designer board games, BGG, and all that jazz.  This game changed that.

I was blown away by how much intensity emerged from such a simple ruleset. As a spy, this game makes me set personal records for dirty, rotten lying.  Not the trivial kind of lying in poker, where you can simply stay quiet and let your chips do the talking.  You have to feign indignance when others accuse you of being a spy.  You have to fake delight when your spy brethren are backed into a corner.  Lots of people just can't stomach this intensity.  I view it as a valuable skillset--one that had lain dormant until I found this game.

The added roles in Avalon do improve the game slightly (although I hear there is an expansion to the sci-fi themed version that includes said roles and more.)  Perhaps even more than the roles, the Lady of the Lake is a very welcome addition, providing a nice amount of concrete evidence to supplement the gut feelings.  But really though, I will never turn down a game of resistance, in any of its incarnations.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I always have just played this as straight resistance so I can't comment on the extra roles and snazziness that distinguishes Avalon from regular old Resistance.  SO this really more of a comment on that game.

Resistance is a great step up from Standard Werewolf.  The first turn is still a little pointless (since the traitors pretty much never reveal themselves in the opening round), but overall it's much more focused than Werewolf.

I personally am not a HUGE fan of this style of game.  I appreciate it for the sort of experience it can bring out and will gladly play it as filler but I get burned out after a couple of games.

The other issue is that newer games of a similar style are arguably better.  Both Coup and One Night Ultimate Werewolf seem to go further in distilling this "hidden traitor" or bluffing/deduction game down into it's purest and most enjoyable elements. 

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
The best deduction game ever made (*I've played). The game can be as complex or as streamlined as you like because the core mechanics are golden. Muddy things up with Mordred and Lady of the Lake? If you like. Play clean and simple with the 4 base power roles? Sure. The scaling seems very balanced, with things only getting 'goofy' with 9-10 players, but there's a certain fun in goofy oversized games. If you like deduction games, you'll love Avalon.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Excelent design. One of the best games out there. This is the game I've played the most so far (excluding IOS plays and online plays).
We never play just once, we usually play more than 4 times, it's just that good. Even better than 'the resistance'. Awesome game in a small package.

You can play this anywhere, almost no table space is needed. Very few and simple rules. The Merlin (good) and the Assassin (evil) players are always present, and then there are more characters which you can add to scale the game easier or harder for each faction (good or evil). You have Percival, a good player who knows who the Merlin player is, you have Mordred an evil player that Merlin is unaware of, Oberon, an evil player that the evil players don't know who he is, and other special characters. High replayability overall. High recommendation.

RATING: 6
Az első Resistance-hez képest csak annyi újdonság van benne, hogy megjelennek a szerepek, de szerintem ez nagyon nagy különbség! Mi csak a 2 legalapabb spec személyt próbáltuk (5 fővel), de egyszer feltétlen ki szeretném próbálni 10 fővel, több speciális személlyel. Régen sokat gyilkosoztunk. Aki azt szereti, az ezt is fogja. Néhány nagy előnye az Avalonnak (és a sima Resiscance-nek is, bár a szerepek miatt az Avalon közelebb áll hozzá) a gyilkossal szemben:
1. Nem kell egy fix mesélő, mindenki játszik.
2. Nem lehet kiesni a játékból (a gyilkosban nagyon kínos, amikor valakit kinyírnak az elején, és ott ül 1 óráig kukán).
3. Mesélés csak az elején van, így nem lehet 40 perc játék után, az utolsó kör előtt hibás meséléssel elrontani az egészet!!
4. Több kézzelfogható információ van, emiatt kevésbé káoszos, bár ez már ízlés kérdése, hogy valakinek bejön-e.

Nagyon nagy ötletnek tartom, hogy Merlinnek titokban kell tartani a szerepét.

RATING: 7
Avalon is the same exact game as the resistance, with the addition of special roles.
In other words, is a refined, shorter version of Werewolf, without player elimination.

I can see how this game won't charm the hardcore German gamer: it is just a social experience of bluffing, lying and deduction. With a good addition of shouting.

It probably will fall flat with the wrong group, and the first play will probably raise eyebrows with any group... But it still is a good game, short and playable with an unusual range (5-10) of players.

RATING: 9.5
I believe I initially rated this game a 7, but as I have played it more and more I have gradually adjusted my ranking up, up and up. The game really only gets better with time and better as you and the people you play it with gets better at playing it.

Beginners might quickly "give up" if outed as evil and that's the one thing you should never do in this game (unless you really are DEFINITIVELY outed beyond doubt). Once players learn the right mentality for this game it gets beyond awesome. And be sure to use as many of the fun special roles as possible. I like to have at least 7 people playing. If three evil players are needed we will go with Mordred, Morgana and Oberon - if 4 add Assassin. Good always has Merlin and Percival. We really like to play with Lady Of The Lake - especially at higher player counts and Excalibur can be fun too.

For now, the rating stands at 9.5. I'm still reluctant to give it the full 10...but time will tell. For far it has only gotten increasingly better after 91 plays.

One caveat. You need the right group. I prefer to play this with my students (I am a high school teacher). I will not play it with my family. Your family might be different to mine, but this game invites deception, blatant lying, backstabbing and shittalking. Fun, fun, FUN with young people - wouldn't do it with my family. When I started playing this game I was actually terrible at lying. I was OK at playing good, but awful at playing evil. This game has pretty much taught me how to lie convincingly and I am now a pretty good evil player. Maybe not a good thing as such, but lots of fun in the right gaming session.

[i]Edit[/i]: I'm updating this entry. I still love the Resistance: Avalon, and consider it my favorite social game. One Night Ultimate Werewolf and Spyfall are climbing, though. I still think Resistance: Avalon is good for both veterans and newbies, but I've become a little turned off to it with certain groups of people because of how they play. I still play my mind games anyway, bwahahaha. But it does suck out some of the overall fun...


[i]Edit 2[/i]:  Played again for the first time in a while at 6 players, and it reminded me exactly how much I adore this game. 


[i]Edit 3[/i]:  Okay, fine. It's equal to One Night Ultimate Werewolf. One is deeper, one is arguably more pure fun.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
This is a modern classic for a reason. I am a huge fan of Battlestar Galactica and the description of this game as "Pocket Battlestar" is apt. It carries some of the same, fun social misdirection games in a tight footprint of mechanics, rules and gameplay. The only criticism I could imagine for the game that it doesn't seem to have the kind of weight of having your success matter the way longer games like Battlestar do; it plays so quickly that it seems like you're playing about air; the deception is just for its own sake. That said, I can't imagine that anything else would be possible with a game lasting thirty minutes so that's not a fair criticism ultimately. Virtually every gamer should own this title. It fills a niche so perfectly that I can't imagine another title doing so in an improved fashion.

The Avalon version of the game is superior to the original Resistance in every way. Having the Merlin character makes the game so much richer. The theme works a little more cleanly to those new to the game. The mods available are easy to insert and remove. This game essentially creates a richer game of Werewolf with ten or fewer people and deserves its place as a modern classic.

RATING: 8
This is a great party game for a 6-10 player group. It requires a higher level of concentration than games like Werewolf, and the voting mechanic really makes for some fun arguments. I'm listing it as light-medium, but that's debatable. I just know that I'm not a moron, and it still took me 5-ish games to figure out what the hell was going on. And even then, it took me another 10 or so games to start to really grasp the core tactics and strategy. 

This game really tests your memory, and you'll often find yourself doing silent logic problems to weed-out the traitor. To me, it's like having a highly structured game of Werewolf with an equally cool theme.


VERDICT:

If you have a 6-10 person group, you can't really beat this for a filler. Additionally, it's really hard to turn down a game, as they take practically no time at all. I also don't see any reason to play the original, generically-themed Resistance if you have this game as an option. Camelot is a timeless theme that almost everyone loves!

8/10

RATING: 4
I'm just not a fan of the Werewolf-style genre, with the whole secret identity good guy vs. bad guy thing.  The bluff/double bluff thing where there's the constant back and forth of "I'm one of the good guys!"... "no, I'm one of the good guys!", repeat repeat repeat just doesn't grab me.

Now, I do score this better than Werewolf because:

a) There IS room to deduct and actually figure things out potentially in this one.  It's not 100% guesswork based on how you feel you might be reading people.

b) It's short, and therefore tolerable to play for something that I don't really like.

If you like this sort of game, I'm sure Avalon is great.  Just not my cup of tea.

RATING: 4
Merlin RUINS this game. Because Merlin knows who all the baddies are right from the get-go, you HAVE to have a rule that makes up for it to prevent him from being OP. So they do. It's just a sucky, sucky rule.

It feels incredibly anticlimactic when the bad guys win AFTER they've lost the game already just because they guessed who Merlin was.

Guys, if you wanted to have some of the fun of the seer role in Werewolf... you could have just copied the role. Make them guess over the course of rounds who's evil, then you don't need some lameass end game rule to make up for it and even things out.

Apart from Merlin, this game is just The Resistance again with a bunch of variants we've never felt the need to try. Maybe I'll try them someday, but for now I'm happy sticking with The Resistance.

RATING: 8
I was very hesitant to play this as I had played Werewolf many years ago and hated the experience.

I had a great time playing The Resistance though. It adds structure that makes decision making more logical, requires way more cunning, and keeps everyone in the game the entire time. I think the logical aspect - who voted for the mission/mission success or failure, who leaders send on missions etc. spices up the accusations and arguments and requires some really fun metagame aspects - this is a game that demands to be played multiple times consecutively. It is a game that seeds deep paranoia about your own behavior - you constantly think you are betraying yourself. Fun stuff!

I don't often have 7 players who fit the mold for this game, but do occasionally and it is perfect for those situations.

RATING: 6
I do like The Resistance. Not as much as many others as I don’t actively seek it out, but I do enjoy it when I finally play it. I was looking forward to see the changes in this game. After playing, I don’t think I need to own this as I already own The Resistance, but I also think that Avalon might be slightly better due to the various roles. I didn’t care much for the special cards in The Resistance, so I don’t mind that they aren’t available in Avalon. Instead, they have added the secret roles which I found to be quite interesting, though I “only” got to be Morgana and a knight in my two games (oh boy was I glad I wasn’t dealt the Merlin character card as I was playing against guys with tons of games under their belt)! 

One thing I have to say is that the consensus in my big gaming group is that the Assassin is too powerful and that the evil forces often win because of this character; therefore, they play with the rule that the Assassin must make his accusation before the decisive mission! This way the Assassin is more likely to miss. In any case it is a fine game and I guess it’s better than the original Resistance (which you can also play using the Avalon cards, you just don’t have access to the plot cards).

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
I've played both Avalon and Vanilla Resistance hundreds of times.  It is my favorite game system, by far.  I think Avalon is superior to Vanilla Resistance in everything but the theme.

The thing I like best about Avalon is that it has an extreme level of customizability.  You can play Vanilla Avalon with just Merlin and Assassin, or you can have a full-blown Avalon experience by adding in Lady of the Lake, Excalibur, the Lancelots, Mordred, Percival, Morgana and Oberon.  You can use any subset of these and each configuration plays differently.

Moreover, the Merlin mechanic levels the playing field.  Now both sides, minions and knights, have reasons to both lie and deduce.  This makes an already fantastic game of social deduction even better.

Whenever I go back and play Vanilla Resistance now, I just wish I were playing Avalon instead, and so will most likely always want to play it over the base game.

RATING: 8
This is a great social deduction game for large groups.  Though it can be played with as few as 5, I think the sweet spot is 7-10.  If alcohol is involved, the game goes up a notch in my experience.  At least among my groups, people get more invested in winning when a bit tipsy.  The fact that it is in a small package makes it easy to transport.  I think a good social deduction game is a must for any proper board game collection, and Avalon is a dang good choice for that purpose.

RATING: 8
A kerekasztal lovagjai (és Merlin) megpróbálják szent küldetésüket teljesíteni. Ámde beférkőztek közéjük a gonosz Mordred árulói is, akik fő célja Merlin meggyilkolása, de már azzal is elégedettek, ha a küldetést megbuktatják.

Szóval van két csapat: A meg B. A tagjai mind ismerik egymást, B tagjai közül egy kiemelt játékos van (Merlin), aki tudja, hogy kik az A tagjai. Ha A tagjai rájönnek ki Merlin a játék végén, mindenképp ők nyertek. Ha az 5 körből álló küldetések közül legalább 3 megbukik, szintén az A csapat nyer. Ha 3 küldetés sikerül és Merlin nem bukik le, B csapat nyer. Ez az alapjáték, ezt lehet bonyolítani további szerepekkel amik még asszimetrikusabbá teszik az információk áramlását.

Nagyon jó kis hazudós, titkos szerepes játék, persze - mint a Secret Hitlert - ezt is jobb többen játszani. Minél többen, minél több extra szereppel, annál jobb.

RATING: 7.5
For fans of The Resistance, this version is mostly the same - two secret teams working against each other to be the first to complete (or sabotage) 3 missions.  Obviously it's all been rethemed here to quests, knights of Arthur, etc.

There are 2 main differences.  The first is that the plot cards from the original game have been removed, but there is info in the rules on how to add those to add to your experience here.  Secondly there are a number of new specific roles added, which can be included or not depending on what layer of complexity the group can handle, and if you want to try and bias things a bit toward good or evil.

Definitely fun, I'm really glad we got to try it, and I appreciate the extra attempt made to balance the scales of power.  I think it's questionable if you need to own both games, but I think any fun group needs one or the other.

RATING: 9.5
Very simple rules, but incredibly deep learning curve. This game is all about logic, people reading, empathy, leadership, and of course bluffing!

There are so many different and unexpected situations that make Avalon so fun and create nearly endless replayability. This game is not really about the game, it's about the people you play with.
Me and my friends used to play Jaguar's Friend, Werewolves, and Mafia, which are all similar. We loved Avalon so much, that on our first day we played FIFTEEN games in a row.

It's also excellent to play with a lot of people. It can hold from 5 to 10 players, games are pretty quick (usually 20 to 40 minutes), and everyone plays from the beginning to the very end. And the best thing: most of the times you'll never completely understand what's going on until the very end!

UPDATE:

Will maybe update the rating as I think it will only shine with +7 players

GOEDE KARAKTERS :

Merlin : hij weet wie de spionnen zijn en probeert de andere goede spelers tips te geven over de identiteit van de spionnen. (voordeel voor the resistance)

Percival: hij weet aan het begin van het spel al wie Merlin is. (voordeel voor the resistance) 

SLECHTE KARAKTERS :

Assassin : hij mag op het einde van het spel gokken wie Merlin is. Als zijn gok juist is, winnen de spionnen. (voordeel voor de spionnen)

Mordred: zijn identiteit blijft geheim voor Merlin. (voordeel voor de spionnen)

Oberon: hij weet niet wie de andere spionnen zijn en de andere spionnen weten ook niet dat hij een spion is. (voordeel voor the resistance)

Morgana: zij verschijnt in het begin van het spel als Merlin. Zo weet Percival niet wie van beide (Merlin of Morgana) de echte Merlin is. (voordeel voor de spionnen)

RATING: 8
Players are members of Arthur's inner council, heading out on quests and fighting evil in the kingdom.  

This is a new version of the superb The Resistance.  The game play is essentially the same - a group of loyal followers has been secretly infiltrated by evil, who are attempting to topple the council from within.  All roles are hidden, so paranoia reigns here.  The first to complete/sabotage three quests wins the game.

This version has added in the characters of Merlin and the Assassin.  Merlin knows who the evil players are, but has to stay hidden as the evil players have a chance to win the game if they identify Merlin correctly (this is the Assassin's role).  Several other characters - Morgana, Percival, etc - can be added in to spice it up even more.  

If you are a fan of The Resistance, you'll want this.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
This is an "updated" version of The Resistance, with more roles which bring neat little twists to the game. So, this is a hidden role game, where every player gets assigned (randomly and secretly) either the role of a bad guy or a good guy. Once everyone has looked at their cards, everyone closes their eyes and, when called for, the evil guys open their eyes so they can see who they will be playing with. Once this is done, everyone closes and then opens their eyes at the same time. One player is then chosen as "team leader". He will select from 2-5 players to go on a mission, contingent on how many players are playing (up to 10!) and whether or not it is mission 1 to 5 (the amount of agents increases as the rounds proceed). There is a vote by each player to see if they agree with who will be sent out, and if the majority agrees, the team attempts the mission (or quest in Avalon). Each of the player selected for the mission receives two cards - Success or Failure. They then select one card and discard the other one *without showing anyone*. Once each member of the team has made their selection, the cards are shuffled (to hide who played what) and are revealed. Should they all be Success, the mission was successful. Should there be even one Failure, the mission went south and failed. The good guys are trying to get 3 Successful mission while the bad guys are trying to get 3 Failed mission. So far, so Resistance. Now here comes the wrinkles: instead of being generic good guys/bad guys, there are specific roles, such as Merlin, who gets to know who the bad guys are, but! if the bad guys successfully identify him at the end of the game, they win, even if they didn't get their 3 Failures. There is also Percival who gets to know who Merlin is. He should only be played with Morgana, who can pretend to be Merlin when Percival gets to find out. This can cause lots of laughter and confusion during the game as Merlin tries to hint at who the bad guys are without letting anyone know who he is since he might get killed at the end, thus losing! And Percival who sort of knows who Merlin is but not really! There's other roles too, but the only other one we played with was Lancelot... or rather the two Lancelot, one who is good and one who is bad. The thing is... they can change place. At the start of any mission, you flip a card. If it is blank, nothing changes, but should it show the two Lancelot, the good one becomes evil and the evil one becomes good. Lots of laughs, lots of fun, will be bringing it again. Fun fun fun.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
I got this game as a gift. I had been looking for a Werewolf style game that worked with fewer players, and it did not disappoint. I love this game because it's all about making crazy unfounded accusations, and then trying to convince people they make sense. Although it's frustrating to be the target of accusation, it's just fun to experience how group opinions are shaped and manipulated. This game works well for talkative, thick skinned groups. As the villians, you really have to believe that you are a good guy until the second you vote. This game has proven that I am a terrible liar.

We like to play where the mission leader describes what the mission is. This adds some more thematic flavor and give something else to argue about.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Probably the apex of the social deduction genre. Figuring out the combinatorial relations of who's voting where and who's passing what requires enough thought to make the deduction interesting.

That said, the game isn't really winnable using only that style of deduction; it requires predictions and extrapolations of other player's behavior and potential behavior. In fact, reading other's behaviors in this way is probably the most central part of the game. This is a skill, and it's one that it's possible to get better at.

The game's focus on reading does have downsides: the game shouldn't be played with uncaring players, and skill development is prone to confirmation bias. The first problem particularly rankles, as the game is simple in principle and can be introduced in lots of social settings, but is likely to go over poorly with some participants. A player who legitimately doesn't care brings the entire game down, and that's likely to occur in the social settings the game should slay in.

The confirmation bias isn't entirely a problem, though. Players' tendency to overestimate their own knowledge makes the final reveals all the more tense, and it's that final reveal that makes the game.

The included mix of roles and Lady of the Lake card do improve the game. Because of the game's tendency to groupthink, the roles' bias toward one side or another allow tweaking of the experience in a positive way (unlike many grab-bag expansions that just confuse players). As far as I can tell, all the special roles are worthwile, and well worth including in the box (if not your first game).

RATING: 7.5
I rate and consider both Resistance and the Avalon version as if they were one in the same - I always play Resistance with Merlin/Assassin (barring brand new groups) and I never play Avalon with anything more than Merlin/Assassin (I don't have any group who's interested in exploring these other routes.)

I would always take a game of Deception over Resistance.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Pretty much the exact same as Resistance, but the addition of the role cards is high-impact, so much so that they rolled them back into the base game.  Of these, I think the most important addition is the Merlin/Assassin combo.  It makes you wonder why they weren't part of the base game to begin with as they add an extra layer of secrecy and mistrust to the table.  

Knowing that there is absolutely someone out there who knows everything at the table before the game starts (Merlin) is superbly balanced by the need to stay hidden from the one player who can ultimately clutch win it for the spies (Assassin).  For the players, play goes on as normal, but you're also trying to suss out who the Merlin is so you can vote with confidence; for the Merlin and Assassin, it's a nice little extra game of cat and mouse as the Merlin wants to tell everyone who the spies are, but cannot do so for the threat of the Assassin.  It's a beautiful edge to the game.

FYI: The Merlin starts the game knowing who the spies are.  The Assassin's job is to kill the Merlin; doing so wins the game for the spies, regardless of the outcome of the missions.  This can happen after the game has ended.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Oh Avalon, how I love/loathe thee.  I could write an essay on this one, and the psychology behind it.  This is a fantastic hidden identity game, and one with extremely high replay value, at least in certain circumstances. I've had more fun playing this game than just about any other--but it can be extremely, extremely frustrating, too. 

The key to a successful Avalon is having a large group of people (7+), and they must be repeat players--much of how this game is played depends on each individual group and the customs and signals the group develops.  This is a game of wits and a game of bluffing.

Two notes:  (1) Boardgamegeek's classification of Avalon as a "party game" is selling it very short.  There's a lot going on here.  (2)  As an aside, if you play this game with any frequency, you will get really good at looking people straight in the eye, and telling them the complete opposite of the truth.

RATING: 3
[3 plays] The people who taught me this game didn't mention up front that it was a re-theme of the Resistance, and I sat there during the explanation thinking "wow, this seems JUST like the Resistance!" Not until I saw the BGG listing did it all make sense.

Anyway, this is just like the Resistance! But with an Arthurian theme, which is probably a slight improvement. And it's probably a fine game for what it is, but this was the game that finally made me realize that I just don't like this kind of game. 

I love deduction games, but not these "social deduction" games. They're probably more interesting the better the players know each other and the more they have played together, and since they are not popular in my circle, I didn't see them at their best by only playing occasionally. There's only as much to these games as the players bring to them, and without good player input, they're boring and random.

RATING: 6
A party game that adds mechanics similar to Werewolf to the negotiation/deduction of Resistance. Theme-less gameplay that rests solely on the meta-gaming of one or two Alpha players that eventually makes the gameplay stale and unappealing. Negotiation games and co-op games in general need a higher level of theme and tangible intermediate goals to keep my interest.

They also depend on each player having a clearly defined turn where they act on their motivations and command center stage without being dominated by the meta-game of the game mechanics and the Alpha players.

RATING: 8
My only negative comment on vanilla Resistance is that I miss the roles/powers of Werewolf and then BAM, they come out with Resistance: Avalon.  Takes some familiarity with the game to be able to play successfully as Merlin (or one of Arthur's knights too, actually), but I would never play vanilla over this unless the majority wanted to for some reason.  Assassination of Merlin gives awful spies like me a shot at redemption :)

RATING: N/A
[b]Sold[/b]
The Resistance (and by extension, Avalon) was largely supplanted for me by Secret Hitler.  The latter game has more ability to play the probabilities to try to figure out who is a bad guy, rather than Avalon, which largely seemed to devolve into an analysis of who deviates from the accepted meta game.

I found Avalon to regularly go too long, and had far too many games where the discussion was more about whether you are "playing the game right" rather than about actually playing the game.  I get why some groups can get obsessively deep with Avalon, but it's one of the worst games I can imagine playing that many times.  It's the sort of thing that would just suck the fun right out of a game for me.

RATING: 6.5
Pros
-Social game based on deduction, logic and reading others
-Flexibility in which characters you can opt to use
-Fair game length
-Low/no setup, portable
-Good replayability

Cons
-Relies heavily on group; not for everybody (lots of arguing, betrayal etc)
-Harder to explain than Resistance because of character powers and all hidden information
-Bad luck can ruin a game (e.g. good guys finding their perfect combination on their first try)
-Consequently, can feel very luck based (especially an issue if not many powers are used)
-Minimum group size is restrictive (NEEDS 5+)

RATING: 7
I really enjoy the game. It plays super fast, a round takes maybe 15 minutes on average, but we can play this for hours. And the characters are awesome! It is a very tough game for the good guys, but it's much better so than if it were vice versa. Word of caution: This is a hidden agenda game and is therefore very confrontative and is more enjoyable with a talkative group.

In comparison to other iterations of games of this genre, it is not that different IMO. For me the best thing is that it takes a short time. However, the one thing I don't like at all is the generic fantasy theme. That can be a serious turn off for people who are not that keen on these stuff, myself included. As a game intended to be enjoyed by non-gamers as well, I think that a more inviting art/theme would have been better.

RATING: 4
5-10 players, best with 7-8

Not my game.  I find the main voting mechanic repetitive and the game dull as dirt.  That's especially true if you don't get a named character and/or you aren't often selected to go out on missions.  I'm not into party games in general, although I enjoy Dixit, Cards Against Humanity, Shadow Hunters, Bang!, Infected, and Salem 1692, but this is one of the lowest on my list.  I'd be fine with the voting mechanic if it serviced something else that actually featured gameplay, and not just a second pass/fail vote.  But voting to service more voting, all to service an identity enquiry just doesn't do anything for me.  Add to that the lying component, which I don't have a moral problem with, but which I actively dislike doing, just means that this game fails for me on all levels.  I'm in a gaming group that loves this game, and I'll play it with them if I'm in the mood and because I like the people in the group, but I'd never buy it, never suggest it myself, and just as often I'll diverge from the main group and go play something else just to get away from this game.

Pros:

RATING: 1
Although I didn't have as miserable an experience playing this as I did Nightfall, The Resistance is still one of the least enjoyable experiences I've ever had playing a board game. My bad experiences include (but are not limited to): Not going on any missions for an entire game because I was a traitor in the last game (I had literally no interaction in the game whatsoever) and another where "I don't even know this guy, so I'm going to vote against everything he does". There are no meaningful decisions, the game revolves around people yelling at each other and lying about whether or not they can be trusted - I'm neither loud nor a good liar/bluffer, so this game holds absolutely no appeal for me.

I will never play this again, however I do understand why some people like it. I rate it this low because I don't really consider it an actual game, just an activity (and one that can be horribly broken by people who know each other and can tell when each other are lying).

RATING: N/A
5-10
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
[b][i]The Resistance: Avalon[/i][/b] is a fun quick lie-to-your friends social deduction game. Everyone goes through the game claiming to be a good guy while a few are actually bad guys lying through their teeth. People vote on a subset of the group to send on a mission and, if sent, bad people will sometimes cause the mission to fail while claiming that they would never have failed that mission. Games sometimes come down to shouting matches, but in a good way. It's the only game where I feel comfortable sitting down with 9 complete strangers and telling one of them (while smiling to remind that it is, after all, only a game) that I think they're a dastardly no-good liar, an evil Minion of Mordred bent on sowing the destruction of all that is good and virtuous. They of course accuse me in kind (probably correctly) and by the end you've hopefully made some new friends.

Because comparisons to Mafia/Werewolf (another lie-to-your friends social game) are nearly inevitable, I'll add that I think The Resistance is superior in every possible way.

[b]Avalon vs Standard:[/b] I think The Resistance: Avalon is better than The Resistance. They both have the same core rules, but Avalon has alternate identities instead of once-a-turn action cards. The one thing I prefer in The Resistance is the dystopian future theme. Still, you cannot go wrong with either.

◊s◊

RATING: 9
This is the best party game I own when it hits the table.  Certainly have seen people hold grudges from it, but man, it's just a great version of bluffing/hidden info.

Things I particularly like:
Every person is important.  You don't have a have the merlin card to be relevant in a game.
The design of needing to know the exact right good team by the end of the game.
Components feel nice.  I sleeved the cards, as I think they were so-so, and I didn't want them showing marks, but the rest of the components are great, feel nice and slick.

RATING: 8
A really brilliant game when played in large numbers.  The arguments around the table about who to send on a quest are heated and often hilarious.  With smaller groups it loses some of its fun and becomes a bit more serious, as you can start to logically work out who might be the traitor.  In large groups that's almost impossible to do at times and it turns a bit more into a game of poker, trying to read your opponents and pick out any bluffers amongst them.

RATING: 8
Szilveszter alkalmával sikerült kipróbálni ezt a partijátékot, pedig már korábban is megkaptam Jani barátunktól PnP változatban, II. világháborús kémes design-al ajándékba.
Nagyon tetszett, nem hiába szerepel vezető helyen a vonatkozó listában.
Nagy előnye számomra a "gyilkolós/vérfarkasos" játéknál, hogy játékideje jóval kevesebb, így több játékra lesz alkalmunk, több lehet a sikerélmény. Ajánlom betenni a nevesített mellékkaraktereket is. Profik részére az akciólapok tovább színesítik a játékot.
A játék egyetlen gyenge pontja maga a játékos társaság. Csak olyanokkal ülj le egy asztalhoz, akik tényleg szeretnék kideríteni, hogy kik a kémek, van kedvük a játék közben figyelni a többiek reakcióit, döntéseit, maguk is aktívan részt vesznek benne. Ezért is partijáték! :)
Összességében remek szórakozás!

RATING: 9
Logic & reasoning.  Backstabbing and Betrayal.  Those are the best descriptors of this game and you should be prepared to despise your friends for lying to you at the end of it.  

Based in Arthurian legend, Avalon requires the Knights of the Round Table (5-10) to go on quests for Arthur in order to defeat the forces of Mordred and Morgana.  However, the Knights have been infiltrated and some are secretly working to Mordred's cause.

Minimal number of gameplay pieces so it's quite portable and the only thing you need to bring with you is a brain and an ability to lie.  The different characters are optional but keep the game fresh with the different number of combinations that can be played.  Card protectors are advisable.

Best not to play with lots of alcohol as people can become quite arsey.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
While Avalon is very good for what it is (a Werewolf/Resistance/Mafia/Bang! type game where you are given a secret identity and two teams try to influence each other without revealing themselves) I dislike all of these games and Avalon is no exception. Every one of these games relys on deception and accusation (all within the scope of the game), and I am very uncomfortable with lying and accusing so I don't enjoy it. These are also behaviors that I would rather not encourage in my child who is frequently at my game nights, so that's another factor. A friend commented recently that "Avalon is a game where you feel dirty if you win, and dirty if you lose" and I agree. 

All that aside, if you do enjoy this type of game, Avalon is certainly one of the best versions out there. Players don't die or get eliminated until the end of the game so everyone remains involved, and there are optional special characters that you can play with to add some interesting twists. (Percival knows who Merlin is, and the Lady of the Lake can learn the good or evil nature of one other player after select rounds). Evil also gets a last ditch effort to win (if they haven't already) by trying to assasinate Merlin at the end of the game.

It is also a good game for a large player count (6-10 players) which can be hard to find, so that is something to consider, but I greatly prefer Codenames if I need a game for a large number of players.

RATING: 7.5
The obvious comparison here is to Resistance, as the only difference here is the existence of specific roles. But I think in total I'm not a huge fan of the roles. I think they're interesting on paper but in practice they just bog down an already strong game. One weird situation is when a non-merlin figures everything out; in the original they still have to convince everyone else whereas here they have someone who can easily just get on their side and know they're right but this then makes the assassin's job basically impossible. Though the opposite could happen as well; a non-merlin could have some theory that ends up being incorrect and they could push it hard, and then that puts merlin in an awkward position and even if the revolutionaries do pull it out, it makes the assassin's life much easier. And it seems like these kinds of situations should come up because the way the merlin/assassin dynamic works, the non-merlins are encouraged to make it look like they know more than they do to throw off the assassin. And ultimately I think all of this gets in the way of what was already a strong social deduction game experience. It's still mostly the same core experience so I do still like it, but I'd prefer to not play with the roles in general.

RATING: 7.5
2012-11-27

Initial Rating: 8.5 (November 2012)

The Resistance Avalon is a better game than the base one. Meaning is it a GREAT negotiation/party game. It adds a lot of complexity with the new characters making it more of a Gamer´s game version of the Resistance. It still has the same core rules, but now you have role powers making it a more compelling experience. Now, both teams have new ways to play with Merlin and the Assassin. The cards and components are gorgeous and in line with the new edition of The Resistance.

With this edition, you can also play the original Resistance, so there is not a reason to buy The Resistance over Avalon. Perhaps, the only caveat to this, is that you can mix the games, I have not read the rules yet so I’m not sure how this will work.

The playtime continue to be short, however with the added complexity comes the main weakness of Avalon. As there are more rules, it is easier to make a mistake that will break the game. In our game, we made 2 mistakes with the new rules and two of us were experienced gamers :S. If you have new players in your hands, I would recommend you to play the original Resistance game before you introduce the role powers.

I dig the fantasy theme, but I prefer the dystopian future of the original Resistance. 

Bottom line, the best iteration of the Resistance series of games. More complex than the original, but more fun too. And you can play the original Resistance with Avalon. A must buy for me (or it would have if I didn’t own already The Resistance, perhaps I will buy it anyway :D)

Current Rating: 8.5

RATING: 10
Incredible game. In my opinion the theme is slighter more fun and engaging than the Resistance and adding the additional characters with unique abilities takes this game up a notch. Overall this is one of the most fun games I've ever played. This was a huge hit with my play group and we could not stop playing! Adding in Merlin (knows who is evil but cannot be too obvious in giving clues to the group because he can be assassinated) and Percival (knows who Merlin is) really changes the dynamics of the game for the better and lessens some of the chance elements inherent in pure resistance. We also had some fun adding in Mordred(stays hidden from Merlin)and Morgana (reveals herself to Percival as Merlin) although we found Morgana very challenging to play effectively.

RATING: N/A
[b][url=https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/1116727/2013-golden-geek-awards-nominees-announced-voting]2013 Golden Geek Nominee[/url][/b]

The Resistance: Avalon pits the forces of Good and Evil in a battle to control the future of civilization. Arthur represents the future of Britain, a promise of prosperity and honor, yet hidden among his brave warriors are Mordred's unscrupulous minions. These forces of evil are few in number but have knowledge of each other and remain hidden from all but one of Arthur's servants. Merlin alone knows the agents of evil, but he must speak of this only in riddles. If his true identity is discovered, all will be lost.

Players: 5, 6, 7, 8, 9, 10
Time: 30 min
Mechanics: [property=1023][/property], [property=1039][/property], [property=1026][/property], [property=2019][/property], [property=2020][/property], [property=2015][/property], [property=2017][/property]

RATING: 10
The Resistance really is the greatest negotiation game currently in existence and the new version has pushed me to finally upgrade both the base game and the new version up to a 10.

I don't care at all about the theme, which to me seems superfluous and hackneyed. I didn't care about the Star Wars-ish theme either, but I think the idea that a King Arthur theme makes the game more approachable to the general public is also silly. It also is very surprising that they would let the game go to print with the typos on the cards. I don't really care, since they don't affect the game play at all (no one has even noticed them), but I do think it is unfortunate.

I also disapprove of the Kickstarter model, which encourages companies to hold back parts of what must have been originally part of the game to reward backers. There's no reason why Lancelot shouldn't be part of the game that everyone purchases except greed. That said, I have no principles in this matter because I still backed the project because of my love for the game.

I have enjoyed Resistance at all player counts. It is relatively easy to teach and with seasoned players, it is one of the most intense game experiences you can get. The amount of deceit flying around the table is really tons of fun. One of the hallmarks of a great game experience is how much it is discussed once it's over. I've seen conversations go on for quite some time about what had just happened, which goes to show how rewarding the game is.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Avalon makes it hard to enjoy other hidden identity games.  I would like Secret Hitler if it wasn't for Avalon.  I can't play the Resistance anymore.  Avalon just does everything so well.  There is an elegance to it that the other games lack.  Currently, the only other hidden identity game that I will choose to play over Avalaon is Rick and Morty: Total Rickall, but that's only because I'm a fan of that show.

I love this game, but having played it several times a month for over a year, I have to take a break.  The key is moderation.  There are other games that I really want to play that I miss out on when I play too much Avalon.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8

4 players:
1 minion (assassin)
3 loyals (2 normal and Merlin)

4 rounds:
Round 1: 2 players
Round 2: 3 players
Round 3: 3 players
Round 4: 3 players

Loyals needed 3 successes to win, minions only needed two.

RATING: 8
[PNP] One of my first social deduction games and I still occasionally play it. Secret Hitler kinda replaced it but I'll talk about the strengths of this one. First of all picking a team of 3-4 players is crazy tense, everyone is looking at you and lying shamelessly or they are telling the truth and you have no idea. When you get betrayed and get blamed you just feel the pressure to defend yourself and find the evil person that just flunked the mission. The special abilities also add some flavour to the game. I still like this one and want to play it when we are 7 players since it is the sweetest number for it. Maybe get Secret Hitler over this if you don't own any of them even though this is cheaper.

RATING: 2
Supposedly a more balanced version of Werewolf/Mafia that doesn't need a moderator and doesn't have player elimination. Thing is, it's balanced to an extreme. I enjoyed my first couple games, but repeated plays have proven to be less and less fun. Once you are familiar the game, it basically plays itself, not to mention some mechanisms are easily exploitable.

To put things into perspective, I have more fun getting eliminated in the first round of Werewolf, and then spending the next half hour quietly observing the group dynamics, than playing Avalon from start to finish. Maybe Werewolf is unbalanced, but the actual experience is fun. The one Avalon crafts isn't.

Rating: :star::nostar::nostar::nostar::nostar:

RATING: N/A
The Resistance: Avalon pits the forces of Good and Evil in a battle to control the future of civilization. Arthur represents the future of Britain, a promise of prosperity and honor, yet hidden among his brave warriors are Mordred's unscrupulous minions. These forces of evil are few in number but have knowledge of each other and remain hidden from all but one of Arthur's servants. Merlin alone knows the agents of evil, but he must speak of this only in riddles. If his true identity is discovered, all will be lost.

Better then Werewolf as it is for less people and more of a sit down (controlled game). Also better then The Resistance for me due to the diffident characters.

RATING: 7
A game about deception and deduction. Two teams race for best-out-of-5. "Good" players must try to learn the identities of others, while the "bad" players knows the identities and are trying to confuse the "good" players. The game requires a LOT of table tall, information sharing, and each player should feel comfortable about lying. Very mind-tiring game and requires everyone to be at the same level, else it would be a frustrating game. 7+ players recommended.
The base game is identical to The Resistance, however the special character powers adds to the replay value, as well as level of deduction. Could argue it is strictly better than The Resistance.  

Replay Value: 4
Difficulty: 2.5
Time: 30-60 minutes

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
This is a significantly, much better enhancement/ implementation of The Resistance, with an extra layer of social strategy using special role cards (like Werewolf).  Avalon has more social intrigue than Werewolf does and does NOT require a non-player moderator!  It also adds the flavorful theme of Camelot.  It probably could've been called "The Mists of Avalon" b/c that's how it feels when you start out each game - most players are in a fog as to who is really whom.

In my first playing of it, it quickly became very addictive and the majority of our group proceeded to play over 7 times in under five hours!  This rocks if you really enjoy social deduction & hidden/secret roles in games like Werewolf, Battlestar Galactica, Shadows Over Camelot, Shadow Hunters, Bang!, etc.  (I daresay Resistance Avalon is probably way better than Werewolf within the 5 to 10 players range since it's the same feel, more social deduction opportunities and in a shorter game time plus there are no player eliminations.)

RATING: 9
after 8 plays
The best at what it is, a bluffing social deduction game.

Easy to learn, difficult to master, the ever-evolving game states change with whoever you play and roles they get along with their reactions.

Lots of variants combination to tune the balancing for each geoups
ie. Mordred in to help the bad guys, Oberon in to help the good guys etc.

Require the group to speak up their opinion.
Require Merlin to not break the game. The newbies would find it difficult at first but they can learn it the hard way, just reset the game if that giveaway is too strong.

Great time without ever dragging too long.
Can be good for people to get to know each others.

Highly recommended.

RATING: 9
The Resistance: Avalon is a superb secret-roll/secret-objective, hidden power, bluffing and deduction type card game (what a mouthful).  In it, players are dealt a character card that is kept secret.  The character cards will either be those of the good guys, i.e. members of King Arthur's court, or the bad guys, i.e. members loyal to Mordred.  Some of these characters may have a special ability.

During each round a player will act as the "King".  The King decides who to send out on missions.  Once the King has chosen who will go on the current mission everyone votes to pass the team selected.  If the vote passes those members chosen will carry out the mission, if the vote fails the mission is rejected.  In that case the player to the left becomes the new King, and the mission selection and voting process begins again.

The players selected to go out on a mission will then secretly chose from "success" or "fail" cards to determine if the mission worked out for the good guys, or not.  Once all cards are handed in they are shuffled and revealed.  For the mission to be a success everyone who went on it must have played a success card, but only one failure is required to ruin the plans of Arthur.  Good guys must vote for a success, but those devious baddies can strategically vote either for a success, or fail.

There are five missions total.  Three successes wins it for the good guys, three failures wins it for the bad guys.  Also, if the mission selection vote fails to be passed 5 times in a row the bad guys immediately win as well.

The Resistance: Avalon is a fast and fun game.  The difficulty can be modified by using more or less characters with special abilities.  The game is tense almost from the beginning.  If you're good you don't know who to trust, unless you are Merlin who knows the evil players.  If you're a bad guy, you are always trying to deflect suspicion away from yourself and onto others.

If you like this kind of game and don't own it already - buy it now!  If you are curious about getting a game like this The Resistance: Avalon is a great one to get first.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.9
Perfect social deduction game... Original Resistance took the BSG traitor mechanic and turned it into a great game. Avalon adds some special roles (bit like Werewolf) to the mix bringing the system to whole new level. Hard to return to basic Resistance after trying this. Lots of fun for 5-10.

Update:
With expansions, original Resistance again becomes the ultimate version (see my comment on it).. But I still recommend Avalon as a better gateway into Resistance, as it has better theme and Merlin+Assassin roles are enough for newbies anyway. And if you don't become a huge fan, this version is more than enough for occasional game or two.

Travis says: 

You may or may not have heard that there was a small misprint on two of the character cards. These cards are the special (and optional) characters Mordred and Oberon. The cards should have had the subtitle "Unknown to Merlin" and "Unknown to Evil", instead they say "Unkown to Merlin" and "Unkown to Evil" respectively. This misprint in no way affects game play.

RATING: 8.25
A game of two teams trying to work together against each other.  The baddies are outnumbered but know who they other baddies are.  The goodies (with one exception) don't know who are on their side.

This leads to some great bluffing, deduction and social interaction.  Accusations abound as both sides try to get their players on to the missions to complete or sabotage them. Plays very differently depending on the group of people played with.

This version of the Resistance comes with some cards that can be used to scale the difficulty in either direction if once side has an advantage in a particular group.  Can also be used to add complexity if desired.

Nice artwork and theme, just be sure to sleeve the cards so they don't get marked (which could give away who your character is).

RATING: 5
A good social deduction game, with more of an emphasis on lying / deceit. The mastermind-quality of the deduction aspect works but is a simple framework complicated both by the open voting (at least that's how I played) and the possible roles (Merlin & Assassin in the games I played). I like it, about the same as One Night Ultimate Werewolf if not just a notch below (subject to change with more plays, currently I've played ONWU much more than I've played Resistance). It is longer, but that is not a bad thing in this case, as you invest yourself more in the outcome and people are just more on edge than in the single rounds of ONWU - I suspect that the odd numbers 5, 7, 9 make for the best games, as opposed to 6 (the way I played) which felt slanted towards the Resistance. Either way, you need people who won't just sit mute but really engage vocally with each other to make this game shine - and win or lose it's fun to unravel the game after to hear what everyone was thinking and why. Even without roles, just bare-boned, this game is very solid and I can't really see room for tinkering with the setup except for said roles.

A good game.

RATING: 10
If The Resistance fixed the Werewolf Genre, Avalon perfects it. This game is much more balanced than Avalon with a great check system in Merlin and the Assassin. What's more, you can easily stack the game in favor of the Loyal Knights or the Evil Minions by adding or removing certain roles or adding optional mechanics like the Lady of the Lake. This lets you balance the game with each play to help the side that can't seem to win.  You can even increase the skill level of the game to not just reward Social Negotiation skills, but also reward Card Playing skills by adding power cards from the base game.  And yet, it's stand alone!

One of my favorite Social games ever.

RATING: 1
Broken. 

First 3: Success! Great! Add one more. Second: Success! Yay! Same team! 3-0 victory without effort. This happened almost every time in a 10 player game. The two times it didn't because a spy was lucky enough to be chosen, it was instead a 3-1.

Merlin/Mordred/Percival/Morgana/Assassin are useless as power roles, since their design requires you to play as if they didn't even exist. They all cancel each other out anyway so why bother trying? It's much easier to figure out who the spies are by looking at the votes. Why risk losing the game (it's literally an instant "you lose no matter what" mechanic) on something unreliable?

Rulebook and cards are full of typos and spelling errors. Did the designer even care?

RATING: 10
The Resistance: Avalon. Able to accommodate large groups, (up to 10,) it's only drawback is it must be played with at least 5. Resistance is a great variation on the traditional Mafia party game. In this version, 2 players are secretly selected to be spies and are known only to each other. The entire group must use successive rounds of voting to hopefully ferret out the villains. The mechanics are simple and quickly taught- it’s the assessment of other players’ trustworthiness, (and eventually the yelling,) where the game really gets exciting. 

Honestly, this is one of my all time favorite games. The Avalon implementation is nice with the Arthurian theme, and the Merlin and other new cards give the game the balance it needs. And if you need the same style of gaming  for fewer players, try Coup!

RATING: 6
Probably the one best quick games I have for a moderately large group of people.  Fast and the tension is frequently palatable.  It can sometimes fall flat based off a random good guess, but that's very rare.  Because this is a bluffing/negotiation game, in essence, it is made by the people.  If you have people that are not in the game and not paying attention then the whole team suffers -- and so does the game by extension. 

As of recently, this game has been nearly completely replaced by Coup (Kickstarter Edition).  Because of the extra cards included with that version of the game, Coup can scale up to being in the same bracket as this game.  Oddly, I find Coup better for smaller (5 or less) and larger (8+) groups, however if in the sweet spot between those numbers then the Resistance might get a chance to shine.

RATING: 6
I can understand why this game is such a hit, but the two games I played weren't very enjoyable. If you have a large group of people who have played it a lot together and a few newbies (like we did), the game can seem pretty confusing and even unfair. The newbies in our group didn't understand a thing and were silent and timid while the veteran players figured everybody out in a matter of minutes. So there wasn't really any negotiating or even bluffing, just going through the motions and number crunching. What this means is that it's good for casual gaming ONLY if you have a balanced out player experience level. It balances a bit If you can play several games in a row, as the newbies get to learn it a bit more, but two clearly wasn't enough. But ours was probably exceptional a situation.

RATING: 7
I bought Avalon because I was intrigued by the simple yet deep deduction mechanisms. Avalon was one of many games that me and my friends brought for a weekend together in the countryside and it turned out to be the only game we played over and over again!

Avalon is learnt, set up and played quickly. The experience does not come from the game as such but rather from the intense interaction between the players. Every action is throughly observed and feriously discussed as each one tries to convince the others who is good and who is evil.

If you enjoy a mental challenge that engage everybody, Avalon is the game for you!

Reviewed at https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/1274558/avalon-party-killer.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.9
主題:1
套用圓桌武士的故事，與遊戲機制的搭配相得益彰，透過每次出任務的成功與否，來判定陣營內的內奸，很有無間道的情節，也很符合圓桌武士故事人物的設定，讓玩家很快就能融入遊戲中。

美術:0.7
圖片美工很棒，看著自己扮演的角色圖案，很能讓遊戲氣氛帶上來。配件很精美，雖然不多，卻算是能對得起這種價格的遊戲。

規則:1
規則簡單好教學，選取角色牌，主持人宣告流程分辨自己的陣營，接著主席選取騎士出任務，騎士決定任務成功與否，接下來就是一連串的爾虞我詐。直到符合玩家人數的任務達成率。遊戲規則讓這款遊戲可以玩得很有邏輯分析性，也可以玩得很搞笑胡鬧。端看玩家桌遊咖的個性取向。曾經跟小朋友玩過，小朋友也超愛的!是一款老少通吃的遊戲。

設置:1
設置很簡單，依玩家人數拿取不同的任務場景圖版，就可以開一局。另外遊戲體積小，很方便攜帶，也是這個遊戲的亮點所在。

路線:0.7
遊戲過程的攻略路線選擇，並不是遊戲制式規定的，而是玩家根據心理學，邏輯判斷，及從與對手的話語間去解讀出誰是梅林方?誰是壞人方?看看是要用虛張聲勢還是順水推舟，或是以進為退、張冠李戴，反正能找出老鼠的就是好貓。這樣海大的策略空間，就看玩家怎麼應用，玩不出所以然的人，只會覺得這是個嘴砲遊戲。

互動:1
遊戲間玩家互動強烈，很多人喜歡當梅林或是殺手，但我覺得最有挑戰性的角色反而是毫不知情的騎士甲乙，要如何從各種蛛絲馬跡中推理出好人壞人，每個玩家的角色都不一樣，採取的策略也不同，而玩家的互動就是從怎麼多的目標衝突中產生。

個人:0.8
陣營遊戲首選﹑，希望能徵得認真玩這款遊戲的夥伴，而不止只是把這款遊戲變成嘴砲歡樂的派對遊戲。

朋友:1
玩過的幾乎都能融入遊戲中，不管是大人小孩。

想玩:0.7
遊戲時間短，主題強烈，遊戲投入感十足，是個可以連開好幾場的微桌遊，
不過玩家人數要五人以上，有時比較難湊咖，且玩多場後，會覺得有點乾，需要一段時間的沉澱再拿出來玩。

收藏:1
價格合理，體積小好攜帶，可以供多人遊玩，每家必備的陣營桌遊。值得收藏。

總分:8.9
講評:除了遊戲策略不夠深入，遊戲玩家限制多人以上外，本款遊戲可說是經典中的經典，相信未來可以常常出現在每個桌遊群中。玩這個遊戲的重點就是要心理投射的將自己融入遊戲角色中，你才會體會到當內奸的快感。

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.5
Hands down this is the most fun social deduction game I have ever played. Actually, this may be the most fun game I have ever played.

It keeps the betrayal mechanism from Werewolf and its ilk, but removes the need for a moderator, player elimination, some of the awkwardness (are we supposed to roleplay this or not?), and puts it in a game that takes only 30 minutes or so to play. Deduction is a much more important part of Avalon (or The Resistance, for that matter), since you can use quest outcomes and team-selection votes to reason about who the traitor probably is.

One of the other things I love about The Resistance and Avalon that I haven't seen elsewhere is that the rulebook explains what roles shift the balance which direction, so if one team is winning too much, you can change which roles you use. That's been very helpful for us, especially since we usually play several games in one sitting, and typically, the balance is a little different for different groups, so we can quickly see which roles to add or subtract to make the game more even.

A few drawbacks: One, there is so much voting, of different types, in this game that new players can easily get confused. For that matter, sometimes, I get confused in the heat of the moment. The other problem is that, since this game relies on votes where every single vote from every player matters, players who are tired or not paying attention can lead to some disastrous outcomes, when a team that should have won suddenly loses because one of its members did something completely at odds with their best interests. But, this factor does not come up very often. Of course, by far the biggest issue in this game is that you have to be able to bluff about your identity - some people (like me) have a hard time bluffing (and in this game, it can feel more like lying than bluffing) and that can be problematic. But that's true of any social deduction game.

Overall, great game; one of the best. If you like social games you will probably like it. If you like games with traitors you will definitely like it. If you like deduction games, you will probably enjoy it. If you like team games you may like it. (The only reason I don't give this game a 10 is because I think it's likely with the rapid pace of innovation in social deduction games that part of the formula may be improved upon, and if some game does manage that, I think it would probably replace The Resistance and Avalon for most purposes.)
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8.3
Love all bluffing games and especially secret identity games. This seems awesome!
Update: Played and own print out version, buying the proper version. Everything about this game is perfect in a genre of games which I consider near perfect. Possibly best of it's type.

like Once upon a time, Aye Dark Overlord, Are you the Traitor/Werewolf, the Resistance or any similar game, these are perhaps my favorite genre of game. They REQUIRE the right group. Right group is a euphemism for people who actually have some inkling of roleplaying, charisma, fun, wit, humor, exuberance, and amicability than this game wins wins wins. Which also means that if your group doesn't like these games, it might be time to get new friends rather than a new group because it's literally their fault and not the brilliant game.

This new version of resistance mostly just adds even better components, better art, and a great new theme. The merlin and other elements are fun; not necessarily worth it on their own unless your a gigantic fan like I am in which case they are.

RATING: 6.5
The issue with the original Resistance was that without plot cards, there wasn't any substantial information to base decisions on, and it could sometimes come to a coin toss. But throw in the plot cards, and you get so much info, the game becomes a game about maximizing the plot cards.

Avalon fixes that with Merlin/Assassin/other cards. M+A gives both the spies and resistance reasons to watch people. Evil wants to find Merlin and assassinate him, while Good still wants to find spies. This adds a whole new dimension and makes the game more interesting for both sides. The other side cards like Mordred, Lancelot, Percival, etc also make the game pretty interesting.

Theres no major issues I have with the game aside from just being bad at most social deduction games and being very tense/stressed under many of them. Minor issues I dislike are closing my eyes, reciting the roles accurately and in order, and the first mission where you have nearly no information. I think apps exist for this though. One way they could have improved this was have text on the character cards briefly reminding the roles, as well as having numbers on each of the character cards, so we could just call the numbers in order. That with maybe a summary sheet of all the characters to keep in the main board. A discard pile wouldn't hurt either.

If you liked this review, I recommend checking out my Resistance review as well if you want a comparison.

Plays: normal Resistance is 25+, Avalon is 5-10+ or so

RATING: 9
This is perhaps one of the best games I have ever played.  I love econ games, strategy games, even war games, but games that play in the air, vice the board just win me over more than anything.  Games where there's intrigue, lying, backstabbing, and laughter all at once is amazing.

Now, I own werewolf, but I have not played it yet.  I own inquisition and play a lot of that.  I also own Bang and Samurai Sword and love those.

But this game beats it all right now.

Everyone wants to go again, everyone has different ways of playing.  Now granted, some people can ruin this game.  Maybe that adds to the theme of the game when someone just doesn't talk or gives terrible direction.  I had a guy who said they were the bad guy all game and when it came to the game winning choice on who went on the mission he says he's good, but no one could trust him, so the good guys lost due to that.

But when the game goes right, everyone is acting good, everyone is vying for trust.  If you can get a group of players like this, this game shines brighter than any game on your shelf.

RATING: 7
抵抗組織：阿瓦隆
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
This is the same game as the Resistance, the only difference being the addition of new characters a la Werewolf. Meaning you can play the original with this set, meaning you would always get this over the original if you were presented with a choice. In the base, the new Merlin knows who the spies are, but the spies don't know who Merlin is. But Merlin can't give the game away, because if the good guys win, the baddies can still win if their Assassin character successfully names Merlin. It adds a great new twist, providing more to think about. There are other characters to add in for even more variety. It makes a great game even better. The theme is non-present, so it's easy to slip back into resistance/spy talk, though you get to enjoy the gratuitous but fabulous artwork for Guinevere. For those who haven't played the original, it's a really fun secret identity game of accusation and counter-accusation, with theories being thrown around on who are the baddies and who are the goodies. The start player nominates who goes on the next mission, which is then voted on, and who votes yay or nay tells you something. If the majority says nay, the next player nominates a new team for a mission. Once the majority says yay, then the players on the mission vote secretly for success or failure. Any one failure and the mission's a failure. 3 failed missions and the spies win. So the resistance players are desperately trying to work out who they are and get them and only them on the missions. The spies know who each other are, and they're trying to fool the other players into getting a spy or two onto missions so they can shoot the missions down secretly. The game really shines when clever bluff moves happen at the start which set up turmoil later and people are all over the shop. It's all over in 15 minutes as well so the time value is excellent, and being able to play with 5-10 players is a big plus as not many games do that well.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.5
40+ plays - Best hidden identity game (in my opinion). A much better version of this game, than 'the resistance'. The roles really add layers to the bluffing, the building of trust alliances and observing 'tells' in other players. The roles are very unique and different to play. Switched on players will begin to observe 'group patterns' that can emerge in a myriad of ways and are not always easy to pick. 

On top of this, it's really a team game. You really rely on the various team members to fulfill their role well, otherwise you lose as at team. This truly is in some ways, a fantastic cooperative experience as well - almost completely immune to alpha players as they will often need to shut up in order for others to play their role (or say a lot to hide the roles of others) :-)
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
This is a fantastic team game and always goes down well when I get enough people together. The short play-time and re-playability make it one of the only games I own which is played multiple times in a row.

It can seem like there is very little information available to the players, especially the Loyal Servants of Arthur, but the more you play the more important and interesting these roles become, as it is really your main job to figure the mystery out or at least make the Minions of Mordred think you know, which can make you look like Merlin.

RATING: 7.8
This game can be very, VERY fun. However, there are a few things that can hurt the experience of this game. 1. Playing with cutthroat players who always play the game with the same strategy and make the bluffing aspect of the game unfun and awkward. 2. Playing with brand new players who don't fully understand the rules. (I've had new players cost us the game by not realizing what they were doing) and 3. You NEED more players. Playing 5 or 6 players is not that fun, you need to have friends AND family to get enough people for this to be enjoyable. Having said all that, play this with a group of people who know how to play the game and just play to have fun, and it's hard to beat. It would have been rated higher if not for the reasons I listed.

RATING: 8
Great party game.  Easy to understand for new people.  Great amounts of interaction.  The only thing that I would say I don't like about the game is that the special character cards can change up the balance in weird ways and that the game doesn't force everyone to make public decisions.  If someone just sits back and never says or does anything, no one has anything to make a decision on their side, whether they are good or bad.  That aside,  I like secret hitler, more because it has more mechanics and it is not solely based on trying to read someone.  I like it.  The pros over Burke's Gambit and Secret Hitler, the two we are currenly playing, is that it scales with player counts better.  Burke and Secret both have issues at the lower player counts.  All in all though this is a good party game that gamers and non-gamers can pick up quickly and enjoy.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Disclaimer: I have not played [thing=41114][/thing].

[floatleft][ImageID=1453087][/floatleft]The Resistance falls into the category of hidden roles deduction games bordering on party game status similar to [thing=925][/thing]. In this standalone successor players are trying to complete quests for the good team to win the game while evil players secretly try to sabotage the quests. One player acts as a leader who assigns certain people to a quest. The players assigned to the quest secretly vote to complete or fail the quest. Players must deduce who is evil from the outcome of the quests. Each turn the leader passes to a new player. All evil players are aware of one another and some characters have special abilities such as Merlin who knows the identity of all evil characters and is on team good. Resistance: Avalon is one of those games where it flubs more often than not but when the planets align and everything falls into place the game absolutely shines.
